## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is central to constitutive modeling in materials science. Temperature typically affects elastic modulus and yield strength, while strain determines the stress through elastic, plastic, and hardening behaviors.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain in elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermally varying modulus)
- Power-law hardening (Ramberg-Osgood type): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening)
- Temperature-dependent power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with thermal softening term)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Temperature-dependent Voce: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with thermal dependence)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening with polynomial strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * exp(c3 * T) (polynomial hardening with exponential thermal factor)
- Hollomon equation with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law in both strain and temperature)
- Swift hardening law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening with pre-strain)
- Hyperbolic sine creep-type: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (thermally activated deformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon))
- Power-law strain hardening → sigma ~ epsilon**n where 0 < n < 1 indicates diminishing hardening rate
- Additive yield stress + hardening → Constant term c0 plus strain-dependent term represents initial yield plus work hardening
- Multiplicative decomposition of thermal and mechanical effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) separable structure
- Temperature-dependent transition → Terms like tanh(c0*(T - c1)) indicate phase transitions or ductile-brittle transitions
- Pre-strain offset in hardening → (epsilon + c0)**c1 accounts for prior deformation history or initial dislocation density
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation in deformation → exp(-c0/T) factor reflects thermally activated dislocation motion

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `99.72829794207104*epsilon*(-0.08976441603442807*(T - 330.599841780566) + 1) + 4.818532892851478*epsilon**3 + 5.41673901332906*(T - 330.599841780566)*sin(epsilon)`

Let me expand the GT:
- First term: `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 0.08976...*330.6 + 1)` = `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 30.674... + 1)` ≈ `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 31.674...)`
  = `-8.951...*T*epsilon + 3159.1...*epsilon`
- Second term: `4.8185...*epsilon**3`
- Third term: `5.4167...*(T - 330.6)*sin(epsilon)` = `5.4167...*T*sin(epsilon) - 1790.5...*sin(epsilon)`

So GT = `-8.951*T*epsilon + 3159.1*epsilon + 4.8185*epsilon**3 + 5.4167*T*sin(epsilon) - 1790.5*sin(epsilon)`

The GT has these basis functions: `T*epsilon`, `epsilon`, `epsilon**3`, `T*sin(epsilon)`, `sin(epsilon)`.

Now I need to check which candidates can produce exactly these basis functions.

Key structural requirements:
1. Must have `T*epsilon` term (linear coupling of T and epsilon)
2. Must have `epsilon` term
3. Must have `epsilon**3` term
4. Must have `T*sin(epsilon)` term
5. Must have `sin(epsilon)` term

Let me check candidates systematically. Most candidates use `epsilon**2` instead of `epsilon**3`, or use `exp()` terms, or `log()` terms, which cannot match.

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `T*sin(epsilon)` - this requires a term that is the product of T and sin(epsilon). Very few candidates have this structure.

Let me scan for candidates with `T*sin(epsilon)` capability:

Looking through all candidates, I need terms that produce `T*sin(epsilon)`. Most candidates have sin terms that don't multiply by T, or have T multiplied by other functions.

- Candidates with `T*c*sin(...)`: Candidate 37 has `c3*sin(T*c4 + c5)` which is sin of T, not T*sin(epsilon).
- Candidate 52: `c4*sin(T*c5 + c6)` - sin of T, not T*sin.
- Candidate 23: `c3*sin(c4*epsilon + c5)` - no T coupling.

None of the candidates have a `T*sin(epsilon)` term explicitly. Can any candidate produce it implicitly?

Looking at candidates with `T*exp(c*epsilon)`: If we could set c1→0, then `T*c0*exp(c1*epsilon) → T*c0`, which gives T but not T*sin(epsilon).

No candidate has the structural form `T*sin(epsilon)`. The basis function `T*sin(epsilon)` is linearly independent from all other basis functions present in the candidates. Since none of the candidates can generate this term, none can match the GT.

Let me double-check by examining every candidate... After careful review, no candidate contains a term that could produce `T*sin(epsilon)`. The closest are candidates with `sin(...)` terms not multiplied by T, or T multiplied by polynomial/exponential functions of epsilon.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), since `T*sin(epsilon)` cannot be generated by any combination of the basis functions available in any candidate, none can match.
